A l l t h e f l u i d mechanics\nd a t a a v a i l a h l e from t h e S k y l a b m i s s i o n s was i d e n t i f i e d and surveyed.\n\'The s i g n i f i c a n t f l u i d mechanics phenomena were i d e n t i f i e d and reduced\nt o measurable q u a n t i t i e s wherever p o s s i b l e . Using e x i s t i n g t h e o r i e s ,\no b t a i n e d from a l i t e r a t u r e s e a r c h , d a t a c o r r e l a t i o n s were performed.\nAmong t h e phenomena a n a l y z e d were: s t a t i c low-g i n t e r f a c e s!lapes,\no s c i l l a t i o n frequency and damping o f a l i q u i d d r o p , c o a l e s c e l ~ c e ,\nr o t a t i n g d r o p , l i q u i d f i l m s and low-g i c e m e l t i n g . A s u r v e y o f t h e\np o s s i 5 l e a p p l i c a t i o n s o f t h e r e s u l t s was made and f u t u r e e x p e r i m e n t s\na r e recommended.\n\nAKO LD E ET\nC N WEGMN\n\nThe authors would l i k e t o e x p r e s s t h e i r appreciation t o the f o l l o w i n g\ni n d i v i d u a l s who contributed t o the data r e d u c t i o l ~and a n a l y s i s : Messrs.\nK . tension\n\np\n\ndensity\n\nu\n\nkinematic v i s c o s i t y\n\n0\n\ncontact angle\n\nQ\n\ndamping c o e f f i c i e n t\n\nw\n\nangular rate, rpm\n\nI\n.\n\nINTRODUCTION\nDuring the Skylab SL-3 mission (tne second manned mission) the\ncrew requested additional scientific activities. Planned\nexperiments were being euccessfully completed at a faster\nrate than expected, due to the diligent work of the crew,\nso they had time for additional investigations. The NASA\nGeorge C. Marshall Space Flight Center defined the objectives\nand equipment for two simple fill-in-experiments. These and\noLher fill-in activities defined by MSFC were categorized\nas science demonstrations since rigorous experiment protocols\ncould not be followed. However, the objective of most of the\nMSFC demonstrations was acquisition of data on basic phenomena that would contribute to the definition of future experiments. Diffusion and ice melting demonstrations were\nsuccessfully performed during the SL-3 mission.\nAnticipating that there would be available time during the\nSL-4 mission, a number of science demonstrations were prepared before the mission. The astronauts performed a large\nportion of the planned demonstrations, whenever their normal\nschedule of activities permitted. These demonstrations\ncovered a wide range of scientific disciplines, but only those\nconcerned with fluid mechanics are discussed here.\nThis was a unique opportunity to demonstrate known scientific\nprinciples in a low-g environment. The demonstrations allowed\na comparison between a typical phenomena, as it occurs in\none-g, and the observed low-g behavior. Low-g theory, based\non the influence of the force of surface tension, has in many\ninstances received very little experimental verifLcation. On\nearth, low-g test periods can be, at best, only one minute,\nwhile in the Skylab a test period of hours was not unreasonable. Since basic principles were involved, ths film data\nfrom the demonstrations makes very good science education\nmaterial.\nBy adding the demonstrations to the Skylab missions an appreciable increase in the scientific benefits of the program was\nachieved at very little additional cost. Hardware did not\nhave to be developed or qualified since equipment available\nin Skylab was used to perform the demonstrations and only\na few small items were taken up to Skylab by the crew. The\nvideotape television system was the prime method of documenting the demonstrations.\n\nThe objectives of the demonstrations were specifically defined.\nHowever, the astronauts were allowed to use their innovative\nabilities in determining the methods and procedures for performing the demonstratione. This approach permitted the\nastronaut to try various approaches if one was not successful,\nand to expand the demonstration based upon what he learned.\nIt provided a change of pace from the usual, carefully detailed\nscientific work of the crew. Only through the effort of the\nSkylat crews were these demonstrations possible.\nThe initial task of this program was to identify and collect\nall the Skylab fluid mechanics data, This data was survhed\nand reduced to a usable form wherever possible. The observations were then correlated with available theory. The\napplicability of these results to various sciences that make\nuse of low-g fluid mechanics phenomena (e.g. space processing\nof materials, cloud physics, cryogenics and space physics)\nwas considered. Finally, future low-g fluid mechanics experiments were recommended.\nAn important part of the effort was a literature search that\nidentified the available theory related to the observed fluid\nmechanics phenomena. From this informqtion, explanations of\nthe observed phenomena were derived. k*ports of the investiwere als. collected and are\ngators on their demonstratio~rs\nincluded in the reference list.\nSome of the fluid mechanic8 data provided by the fluid mechar.ice demonstrations had not been analyzed prior to this program.\nPreliminary evaluations of other portions had been accomplished. In a few cases the data reduction and analysis was\ncomplete, One objective of this program was to review all the\nprior work and to complete the data analyels wherever it was\ndeemed necessary.
